  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cee2a4ac-3f92-4735-9179-fc9bdad7a9f9'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText3683646675293906452" style="display:none">A Warrior without Equal, a Woman without OptionsTriumphs in the Coliseum--and society bedchambers-- made gladiator Alexius of Iolcos famous for his brutal skill and womanizing ways. Yet the only woman who intrigues him is Tiberia the Younger, who now needs his help. Protecting Tiberia places Alexius in the greatest danger he has ever known--from her vengeful father and his own heart...<br /><br />Becoming a temple priestess may be an honor, but Tibi can't bear to surrender her freedom or her newfound faith. Alexius's solution stuns her. Marriage...to a gladiator! Scorned by her noble family, Tibi always felt unworthy. But with her champion by her side, can she accept--and give--a love strong enough to vanquish their enemies?</span>

<div id="review_173062071" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/173062071" />
    <a title="Rebecca A. Rogers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers"><img alt="Rebecca A. Rogers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374240500p2/2824750.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/173062071?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca A. Rogers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca A. Rogers" href="/user/show/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers">Rebecca A. Rogers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/11842776-the-champion">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers?shelf=historical-romance">historical-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2824750-rebecca-a-rogers?shelf=historical">historical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer173062071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17602607522884637520">**ARC Courtesy of NetGalley<br/><br/>I feel the need to insert a disclaimer that this is Christian fiction. Why? Because I know a lot of people who read romance, thinking there will be explicit scenes (which they love). I’m not going to lie—I thought this would have heavier themes, too, but I didn’t let this fact deter me. <br/><br/>The story begins with Tibi, whose father is reckless and demanding. He wants Tibi to find a man to marry, but Tibi is more concerned about her new faith and finding someone whom she lov</span>
  <span id="freeText17602607522884637520" style="display:none">**ARC Courtesy of NetGalley<br /><br />I feel the need to insert a disclaimer that this is Christian fiction. Why? Because I know a lot of people who read romance, thinking there will be explicit scenes (which they love). I’m not going to lie—I thought this would have heavier themes, too, but I didn’t let this fact deter me. <br /><br />The story begins with Tibi, whose father is reckless and demanding. He wants Tibi to find a man to marry, but Tibi is more concerned about her new faith and finding someone whom she loves, not marrying for political or social gain. After several beaus, however, she has unsuccessfully impressed any of them. When her father threatens to send her to the temple to become a priestess, Tibi runs away. Straight to the doorstep of Alexius, a womanizing gladiator and close friend to her family. <br /><br />Alexius has always favored Tibi, and Tibi him. But she could never marry someone like Alexius, who is considered beneath her status. And Alexius can’t marry Tibi because he had promised he’d stay away. The longer they remain together, though, the more they realize their feelings are hard to ignore. <br /><br />The world building of Rome was exceptional. I admit—I’m obsessed with gladiators after watching <i>Spartacus</i> on Starz. Usually, violence and gore are thick when a gladiator takes center stage, but Carla Capshaw abstained from following this road. The themes are definitely there, but don’t go into too much detail. <br /><br />I also like that I connected with the characters. They were both likeable and both made me feel for them (since this is told in different POVs). My only complaint is that it was pretty obvious they were going to fall for each other. But even when Alexius held the party and had women hanging all over him, I felt for Tibi, which says something. <br /><br />Overall, I’d recommend this book for anyone looking for a historical-themed love story. <br /><br />By the way, can I haz the cover model? *drools* :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="17602607522884637520" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_190010553" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/190010553" />
    <a title="Judy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1871221-judy"><img alt="Judy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1349109783p2/1871221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/190010553?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy" href="/user/show/1871221-judy">Judy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer190010553" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7317806362402898537">Carla's roman trilogy is exceptional. I recommend reading all three books. The Gladiator, The Protector and The Champion. They will bring you to a world where blood lust rules, becoming a Christian is like signing your death warrant and where being a woman left you with little power to protect yourself. And that is where we find Tibi, a woman in need of Christ and a champion. <br/><br/>Alexius of Iolcos was the reigning hero of gladiators. His dark good looks and charming personality were as popular outsi</span>
  <span id="freeText7317806362402898537" style="display:none">Carla's roman trilogy is exceptional. I recommend reading all three books. The Gladiator, The Protector and The Champion. They will bring you to a world where blood lust rules, becoming a Christian is like signing your death warrant and where being a woman left you with little power to protect yourself. And that is where we find Tibi, a woman in need of Christ and a champion. <br /><br />Alexius of Iolcos was the reigning hero of gladiators. His dark good looks and charming personality were as popular outside the ring as in. Entertainments were starting to bore him. He thought of his friends, Caros &amp; Pelonia and Quintus &amp; Adiona and their faith. It had changed them but he had too much anger for their God of peace and love to forgive him. He failed his family and the anger needed to be fought even though he now owned the gladiator school.<br /><br />Tibi, Pelonia's cousin, was a disappointment to her father. She could never please him and now she has a fourth broken betrothal and he has threatened to send her be a Priestess at one of the temples. She did not even believe in those gods. Her sister had married a Senator so her father accepted her. She escaped to go find Pelonia but she and Caros had not arrived. Alexius insisted she stay until their arrival.<br /><br />Alexius knew he could never have Tibi. His lower status would not allow it. She needed a champion though and he would be that for her. She had been beaten down to where she could not see her beauty or worth. Alexius could be her physical champion but they were both in need of Christ for the spiritual champion.<br /><br />Received book from NetGalley for review</span>
  <a data-text-id="7317806362402898537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14101429752703146886">Unlike so many historical novels set in the old west, this was a nice change. In the old Roman world of gladiators, senators, and the general mistreatment of everyone the upper classes deem “less than”, we discover the story of Alexius and Tibi.<br/>A little tough to get going, since I hadn’t read the first two stories in what was obviously a series. But I let go the questions that arose over the mention of other couples and focused on what was going on between the two main characters, which kept me </span>
  <span id="freeText14101429752703146886" style="display:none">Unlike so many historical novels set in the old west, this was a nice change. In the old Roman world of gladiators, senators, and the general mistreatment of everyone the upper classes deem “less than”, we discover the story of Alexius and Tibi.<br />A little tough to get going, since I hadn’t read the first two stories in what was obviously a series. But I let go the questions that arose over the mention of other couples and focused on what was going on between the two main characters, which kept me interested enough.<br />Not your usual Christian romance, since neither was preached to during the course of the first half of the book, though they had been in the past. And neither particularly wanted to be a believer until later in the book. Still, it was full of suspense, with a bit of a ‘we’re on the run from the bad guy’ feel.<br />All in all, a good read (quick, since it’s a novella). The reader will find himself bombarded by italics, unable to see the need to emphasize a word for ourselves. (Or maybe I just noticed it more because that’s what my critique group partners called me on recently :-))</span>

  <span id="freeText5879419335377298039" style="display:none">I am in love with Gladiators after reading Carla Capshaw's third book in her Gladiator series. Thanks to the author for sending me a copy!!! I loved the story of Alexius and Tibi. Escaping the wrath a vengeful father leads her into the arms of man she should steer clear of, but God had other plans for both of them. Despite their pasts, they learn to slowly trust each other. It's when the danger of an enraged Father becomes imminent that both learn that only Jesus is their only hope. The fact that Alexius could lose the one woman on earth who has managed to capture his heart is what drives him to his knees and ask help from His maker. The same goes for Tibi. She realizes her need for Christ to fulfill every void her earthly father had left in her. It's through the examples of their friends Quintus and Adonia and Caros and Pelonia that they see how God can truly change lives for the better. Can't wait to read her next book!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy (joyous reads)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy (joyous reads)" href="/user/show/4352734-joy-joyous-reads">Joy (joyous reads)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4352734-joy-joyous-reads?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177779742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2486082140122906585">Ancient Rome believes that women are only worthy of the men they ensnare to marry; powerful, influential men. Tibi is not your typical, obedient Roman woman. And it's not only because she has a fair skin and blond hair, she's headstrong, kind to the poor and the oppressed with a mind and an opinion that she was not afraid to share. But even in her brave countenance, there was only one person who could reduce her to a meek lamb void of any self-importance. Her father had hated her since she was b</span>
  <span id="freeText2486082140122906585" style="display:none">Ancient Rome believes that women are only worthy of the men they ensnare to marry; powerful, influential men. Tibi is not your typical, obedient Roman woman. And it's not only because she has a fair skin and blond hair, she's headstrong, kind to the poor and the oppressed with a mind and an opinion that she was not afraid to share. But even in her brave countenance, there was only one person who could reduce her to a meek lamb void of any self-importance. Her father had hated her since she was born and as she grew into a marriageable age, his disgust toward her became insufferable. She ran away from home and into the most powerful gladiator of the land, Alexius. Together, they fought each other's attraction as it was obvious it was not going to be fruitful. <br /><br />This is my first time reading a book from the 'inspirational' genre. Sometimes, it really is nice to read something clean. It was a shock, actually. I have to say that I was disappointed that this was also a book about gladiator but because of the genre, all the violence and the gore was nearly non-existent here. I mean, the connotation was there but none was described in a succinct matter. <br /><br />The romance proceeded in a snail's pace but the realization of them being in love with each other happened too fast for my taste. <br /><br />The author did a very good job of staying within the parameters of this genre but it's too bad that it took away some of the empathy that I was supposed to have with the main characters. <br /><br />I enjoyed reading this book, nonetheless and I want to thank Harlequin and Net Galley for allowing me to pre-read this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2486082140122906585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2511537-barbara?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2511537-barbara?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2511537-barbara?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2511537-barbara?shelf=ancient-rome">ancient-rome</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer151911499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12711333703771095240">Carla Capshaw's third book in the gladiator series is just as enjoyable as the other two were, if not better! I've tried to think about what makes <u>The Champion</u> such a favorite of mine, and I came up with a few things: The author makes ancient Rome come alive with her descriptions and storyline, and it seems like you are there and involved. Her characters have such a delightful way of interaction at times, with playful, teasing banter. Many other authors today have their characters act like they </span>
  <span id="freeText12711333703771095240" style="display:none">Carla Capshaw's third book in the gladiator series is just as enjoyable as the other two were, if not better! I've tried to think about what makes <u>The Champion</u> such a favorite of mine, and I came up with a few things: The author makes ancient Rome come alive with her descriptions and storyline, and it seems like you are there and involved. Her characters have such a delightful way of interaction at times, with playful, teasing banter. Many other authors today have their characters act like they don't care for each other for most of the book and then suddenly declare an undying commitment at the end, which seems false. Carla's characters don't seem to do that, and their manner of relating to each other seems much more believable. Her "villainous" character in this one made me about as angry as I could possibly be and not decide to quit reading the book. If you haven't discovered Carla Capshaw yet, please give her a try; you will be delighted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12711333703771095240" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_184810299" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/184810299" />
    <a title="Joy " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3676499-joy"><img alt="Joy " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452916428p2/3676499.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/184810299?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joy " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joy " href="/user/show/3676499-joy">Joy </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184810299" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5335492892854673213">Until now, I assumed Love Inspired was synonymous with light romance (not that there's anything wrong with that) but thanks to Carla Capshaw I'll have to mentally re-shelve the line. Sparks started flying in chapter one of The Champion and the romantic tension continued to build making this summer read as refreshing as a glass of iced tea, and not nearly as sweet as I expected. <br/><br/>Fans of the line needn't worry, your favorite Love Inspired authors haven't swapped places with Harlequin Blaze writers</span>
  <span id="freeText5335492892854673213" style="display:none">Until now, I assumed Love Inspired was synonymous with light romance (not that there's anything wrong with that) but thanks to Carla Capshaw I'll have to mentally re-shelve the line. Sparks started flying in chapter one of The Champion and the romantic tension continued to build making this summer read as refreshing as a glass of iced tea, and not nearly as sweet as I expected. <br /><br />Fans of the line needn't worry, your favorite Love Inspired authors haven't swapped places with Harlequin Blaze writers. But if you read a lot of Christian category, you might notice an uptick in the heat level- a fact that wasn't wasted on this edgy Christian fiction lover. <br /><br />Alexius is a gladiator with rage issues, Tibi is the woman who brings out his tender side. Both of the leads were extremely likable, and their faith journeys didn't feel heavy handed. I found the setting and tone reminiscent of Francine Rivers' Mark of the Lion series (but obviously not as graphic). <br /><br />I'm not sure if Capshaw's work represents what we can expect from Love Inspired in the future, but in my best British waif accent, "Please sir, I want some more!"</span>
  <a data-text-id="5335492892854673213" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer451479885" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1754852831583432485">Alexius is amazing. Just saying... While I did not really experience the unsavory side of him, I still saw the fallout of his past actions in a way to make his struggles believable. That he was willing to take in Tibi even though it could cost him his fortune made him a hero in my eyes. He did everything to protect her and to encourage her to be herself.<br/><br/>Tibi was a bit more confusing to me. She had a brutally abusive father yet was uncowed and was beautiful yet did not know it (as many heroines a</span>
  <span id="freeText1754852831583432485" style="display:none">Alexius is amazing. Just saying... While I did not really experience the unsavory side of him, I still saw the fallout of his past actions in a way to make his struggles believable. That he was willing to take in Tibi even though it could cost him his fortune made him a hero in my eyes. He did everything to protect her and to encourage her to be herself.<br /><br />Tibi was a bit more confusing to me. She had a brutally abusive father yet was uncowed and was beautiful yet did not know it (as many heroines are). I guess I would have preferred that she had been more unique.<br /><br />The tension and struggle through the first half of the book kept me staying up late to read as much as I could. This was where I loved Alexius the most and enjoyed the Greek side of him. However, toward the end, I began to loose interest. It seemed to mirror the end of The Gladiator too much. I wish that Capshaw could have come up with a better way to end the conflict than for <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ them to end up in the arena as in the other novella.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><br />To see what books I back, go to my blog at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://backingbooks.blogspot.com/">http://backingbooks.blogspot.com/</a></span>

<div id="review_218247306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/218247306" />
    <a title="Anna Rebecca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5502930-anna-rebecca"><img alt="Anna Rebecca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1430880393p2/5502930.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/218247306?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anna Rebecca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anna Rebecca" href="/user/show/5502930-anna-rebecca">Anna Rebecca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=home-library">home-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=roman">roman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5502930-anna-rebecca?shelf=christian-romance">christian-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer218247306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18092547701762409482">The Champion by Carla Capshaw is part of a series that takes place in Ancient Rome. Ancient Rome happens to be one of my favorite historical settings, and that is what compelled me to buy this book. I’ve not read the other books in the series, but that didn’t at all hinder my ability to enjoy this book.<br/><br/>I must admit, this book surprised me. While the author’s writing style isn’t especially complex, it is still pleasing. I found Ms. Capshaw to be a capable writer and enjoyed her writing style. So </span>
  <span id="freeText18092547701762409482" style="display:none">The Champion by Carla Capshaw is part of a series that takes place in Ancient Rome. Ancient Rome happens to be one of my favorite historical settings, and that is what compelled me to buy this book. I’ve not read the other books in the series, but that didn’t at all hinder my ability to enjoy this book.<br /><br />I must admit, this book surprised me. While the author’s writing style isn’t especially complex, it is still pleasing. I found Ms. Capshaw to be a capable writer and enjoyed her writing style. So often romance writers seem to forget they are writing for adults and not sixth graders. Thankfully Ms. Capshaw gives her readers a bit more credit than that!<br /><br />The story’s plotting was also better than expected. Certainly one can anticipate the plot fairly easily given the genre of book in question. Despite this, Ms. Capshaw managed to keep my attention by throwing in a surprise or two along the way. Though clearly plot devices, I can’t say these twists necessarily detracted from the overall story. In fact, I rather enjoyed them.<br /><br />Ms. Capshaw also proved herself to be capable in her ability to render characters that the reader can care about. Although the characters were formulaic, we are discussing romance after all, they were still had enough originality to make them appealing. I especially appreciated Alexius’ change of heart. The author managed to write the change without making it seem contrived. Likewise, Tibi’s plight, formulaic though it was, still managed to pull at your heartstrings and didn’t seem overly contrived. Kudos to Ms. Capshaw for her ability to render good, likable characters.<br /><br />And, as this is Christian romance, I feel it appropriate to address how the author used Christian themes in the book. What I truly liked about this book was that Ms. Capshaw didn’t feel it necessary to preach at the reader or to dwell over long on Christian aspects of the book in an effort to convert the reader. I thoroughly enjoyed watching Tibi and Alexius come to terms with the Christian faith in natural ways -- ways that could easily happen in real life. At the same time, Ms. Capshaw did an excellent job at showing how salvation “works” in real life. You won’t put this book down wondering how a person comes to a saving knowledge of Christ.<br /><br />Obviously I would recommend this book. I read it throughout the week, but it would be easy enough to read over the weekend if you were so inclined. This is even a book that I would deem safe for the older teen. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18092547701762409482" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_223093326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223093326" />
    <a title="Larena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/785754-larena"><img alt="Larena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316043861p2/785754.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223093326?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larena" href="/user/show/785754-larena">Larena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781459209893" href="/book/show/11531746-the-champion">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223093326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12035007174048341671">Rome AD 84<br/><br/><br/>Tiberia the Younger “Tibi” is about to be sent to become a priestess that many would find to be an honor but Tibi isn’t ready to give up her freedom or her faith. The problem is leaving her will very little options and if she can’t find an answer quickly she is going to end up with a life she doesn’t want. Tibi turns to Alexius to see if he might be able to help though how she isn’t sure of but when one is desperate they are willing to try anything.<br/><br/>Alexius of Iolcos is a gladiator that</span>
  <span id="freeText12035007174048341671" style="display:none">Rome AD 84<br /><br /><br />Tiberia the Younger “Tibi” is about to be sent to become a priestess that many would find to be an honor but Tibi isn’t ready to give up her freedom or her faith. The problem is leaving her will very little options and if she can’t find an answer quickly she is going to end up with a life she doesn’t want. Tibi turns to Alexius to see if he might be able to help though how she isn’t sure of but when one is desperate they are willing to try anything.<br /><br />Alexius of Iolcos is a gladiator that has been intrigued with Tibi for as long as he has known her. Now that she is in trouble he knows that he will do anything possible to help her including offering her marriage so that she will be safe. Though this action will put him in the most danger that he has ever been in, not just from her vengeful father but also from his heart. <br /><br />Tibi is going to have to decide if what she wants because with her noble family this will never be accepted since they only see Alexius and a lowly gladiator. She has always been an oddity within her family and if she does marry Alexius this is sure to make it so that she will never get acceptance from her family. Tibi is going to have to make some decision quickly or she will never have the future she has always dreamed of. <br /><br /><br /><br />This story shows a different side to Rome that most books don’t show readers. For those that enjoyed the show Spartacus they are sure to love this story as it is reminiscent of the show. The characters and details of the places in the story are richly written and will have the reader hating to put the book down for any reason. Once the story draws the reader in it doesn’t let go until the very end. The story gives the reader a glimpse of what the times where like at that time and the turmoil that was happening behind the scenes in the political arena. This one is worth giving a chance as the reader will not be disappointed in the least. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12035007174048341671" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_554797207" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/554797207" />
    <a title="Salyna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10530894-salyna"><img alt="Salyna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597368462p2/10530894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/554797207?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Salyna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Salyna" href="/user/show/10530894-salyna">Salyna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10530894-salyna?shelf=moderate-romance">moderate-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10530894-salyna?shelf=reviews">reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer554797207" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18187540077678485055">Sadly, this was the last of the series. All three of these stories: The Gladiator, The Protector, and The Champion were amazing reads. They all make it into books I would recommend for people who like clean romance and a good story with a little bit of action/fighting in it. I have written a review on my blog for all of them if you wish to stay on my blog a little bit longer.<br/><br/>As you can tell from the description, this book was about the crowds favorite gladiator Alexius of Iolcos and Tiberia the </span>
  <span id="freeText18187540077678485055" style="display:none">Sadly, this was the last of the series. All three of these stories: The Gladiator, The Protector, and The Champion were amazing reads. They all make it into books I would recommend for people who like clean romance and a good story with a little bit of action/fighting in it. I have written a review on my blog for all of them if you wish to stay on my blog a little bit longer.<br /><br />As you can tell from the description, this book was about the crowds favorite gladiator Alexius of Iolcos and Tiberia the younger, aka Tibi. The story was about their secret love for one another growing and in the process their belief and trust in Christ Jesus. <br /><br />I liked how Alexius had a past reputation for "the ladies" and how that made it hard for Tibi to trust him sometimes. It made for some very serious parts in the story where Alexius and Tibi would talk about how things he did could of been mistaken for some thing else, and it made other situations funny because Alexius was a charmer even when he didn't mean to be.<br /><br />The ways that Alexius and Tibi come to know God are so realistic: through friends, past and present experiences, and the natural wonder of their being a higher power. <br /><br />Another thing that I liked was Tibi not thinking she was beautiful even though she was gorgeous. Because of that, Alexius was always complementing her trying to get her to see herself the way he saw her. It was cute and something a lot of girls now can relate to. Almost all girls now days don't think highly of themselves and would kill to have a guy complement them.<br /><br />Once again, and I feel repetitive saying this, but the only thing I did not like about the story was the way it was written in some parts. I lost track sometimes of whoes thoughts I was reading. Other than that it was an enjoyable and fast read.<br /><br />If you would like to read more reviews by me go to: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://kissedbooks.blogspot.com/">http://kissedbooks.blogspot.com/</a><br /><br />Thanks!:)</span>
  <a data-text-id="18187540077678485055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Holly " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1058083-holly"><img alt="Holly " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437576124p2/1058083.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284531621?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Holly " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Holly " href="/user/show/1058083-holly">Holly </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284531621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11264827972869991058">Very good plot, very VERY good plot. 5 stars for that alone. Ancient Rome is one of my favorite era's in history. <br/>However, there seemed to be some kind of disconnect. Firstly The cover seems to suggest it's some kinda trashy porno book. Seems to cheapen the whole thing.<br/>So likes and dislikes<br/><br/>Likes<br/>-How she portrayed the persecution of Christians. <br/>-The two main characters actually had pages of conversation together, so you could see how they fell in love. It wasn't just some "magical glance" and som</span>
  <span id="freeText11264827972869991058" style="display:none">Very good plot, very VERY good plot. 5 stars for that alone. Ancient Rome is one of my favorite era's in history. <br />However, there seemed to be some kind of disconnect. Firstly The cover seems to suggest it's some kinda trashy porno book. Seems to cheapen the whole thing.<br />So likes and dislikes<br /><br />Likes<br />-How she portrayed the persecution of Christians. <br />-The two main characters actually had pages of conversation together, so you could see how they fell in love. It wasn't just some "magical glance" and some "knowning BEYOOOND A KNOWING" they were meant for each other. <br />-As i said, the plot was very good. <br />-The characters, I could see them perfectly in my mind.<br />-The dialogue between the characters, it was really funny.<br /><br />Dislikes<br />-The story just seemed to go on and on and on and on and on and on and on and on....... and on.<br />-Some of the dialogue was so cheesey i was almost gagging on it. <br />-There was a lot of WAAAH WAAAAH nooooobody loooooves meeeeeeeeeeee! from the main female character.<br />-At one point in the story there is a battle between 4 gladiators, which was a total joke because it lasted all of 4 sentences. There was no action to it all. I dont know how she managed to do it, make a fight scene between 4 gladiators boring. That may be somewhat of an accomplishment.<br /><br /> I'm going to read her other books in this series. She's a great writer, I loved her descriptions of roman life, gladiators, villa's, her characters.. it was all very beautifull.<br />Most of all, i love that she wrote how being a christian was so costly in those times. <br /><br /><br /> </span>

<div id="review_200122596" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/200122596?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Niina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Niina" href="/user/show/5740223-niina">Niina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer200122596" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3065505305436944392">Tibi knows what she wants, and she's aware of her worth much to the disappointment of her father, who finally snaps and orders Tibi to the temple of Obis to be a priestess and out of his way. Tibi feels she's destined to marry for Love and not for the political gain of his father, not wanting to go to the temple she escapes to the friend of their family, a gladiator Alexius, a know womanizer.<br/><br/>Alexius had sworn to his friend, cousin of Tibi, that he was to not take Tibi into his bed, she's off lim</span>
  <span id="freeText3065505305436944392" style="display:none">Tibi knows what she wants, and she's aware of her worth much to the disappointment of her father, who finally snaps and orders Tibi to the temple of Obis to be a priestess and out of his way. Tibi feels she's destined to marry for Love and not for the political gain of his father, not wanting to go to the temple she escapes to the friend of their family, a gladiator Alexius, a know womanizer.<br /><br />Alexius had sworn to his friend, cousin of Tibi, that he was to not take Tibi into his bed, she's off limits, which is one of the reasons he feels so stongly about her, but now that she's at his gladiator school he can't help but fall just a little harder for the strong willed, chamelon like girl.<br /><br />I loved this book! I love historical Rome, so this was a perfect match for me! The city and the customs are colored on to the page in a way that you don't for once forget where you are at and with who.<br /><br />I loved Tibi's charcter even though she was still little green around the ears, but she was lovely, quick witted and brave, a very good match for Alexius who was smooth, suave and powerful - and um former gladiator. Yum. ;)<br /><br />This was more of a sweet love story than a hot steamy read, there was plenty of forbidden touches, forbidden emotions and temptation, it was really all about the seduction and not the act itself.<br /><br />If you love historical romance and Rome then this is for you, a beautiful love story definitely not lacking in passion, lust and expectations of the time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3065505305436944392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Gaskins" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Gaskins" href="/user/show/24239244-elizabeth-gaskins">Elizabeth Gaskins</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer728483339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer642263485003863133">The champion is the first Carla Capshaw book I've ever read and I really loved it!<br/>I loved the way that the book bounces from one character's point of view to the others because I love to examine what every character is thinking about the situations rather than just one. What really took my interest though was the amount of love expressed between the two main characters. When Alex <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[goes into her room to rescue her after her father caned her <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> , the amount of love and t</span>
  <span id="freeText642263485003863133" style="display:none">The champion is the first Carla Capshaw book I've ever read and I really loved it!<br />I loved the way that the book bounces from one character's point of view to the others because I love to examine what every character is thinking about the situations rather than just one. What really took my interest though was the amount of love expressed between the two main characters. When Alex <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[goes into her room to rescue her after her father caned her <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> , the amount of love and tenderness Alex expresses in that scene was one of my favorite moments in that book. It is one of the moments that I remember vividly even several months to a year after having read this story. <br />I believe that Mrs. Capshaw is a excellent writer and this story shows it. I would recommend this book to anyone. I liked this book so much that I am planning to look for other books by Carla Capshaw, especially from her books on the Roman gladiator period. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;

      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15630642091993780925">Carla Capshaw is a Florida native who grew up dreaming of traveling the world and writing novels. <br/><br/>After visiting numerous countries, Carla began writing novels in earnest and eventually won two Golden Heart awards as well as a double Rita nomination for her first novel, The Gladiator. Carla loves passionate stories with compelling, nearly impossible conflicts. She's found Inspirational Romance is </span>
  <span id="freeText15630642091993780925" style="display:none">Carla Capshaw is a Florida native who grew up dreaming of traveling the world and writing novels. <br /><br />After visiting numerous countries, Carla began writing novels in earnest and eventually won two Golden Heart awards as well as a double Rita nomination for her first novel, The Gladiator. Carla loves passionate stories with compelling, nearly impossible conflicts. She's found Inspirational Romance is the perfect vehicle to combine lush settings, vivid characters and a Christian worldview. <br /><br />Still living in Florida, Carla is always planning her next trip and plotting her next novel. Visit her at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.carlacapshaw.com">www.carlacapshaw.com</a>. </span>
